Turnout: 50.70% (3,360,330 of 6,627,747 registered).
Biggest gain: đčĐÇđĹ (+44.59 pp). Biggest loss: đôđĽđáđĹ-đíđöđí (-13.00 pp).
Paper / machine vote: 52.39% / 47.61%.
Section-level anomalies detected: 3,331 (recount: 0; machine flash removed: 3,077; problem sections: 138).

## Parties ÔÇö retrospective analysis

Analysis of each party that cleared the threshold on 19 April 2026 ÔÇö what worked, what did not, and strategic notes for the next vote.

### đčđč đśđťđÉ đóđÉđÜđ¬đĺ đŁđÉđáđ×đö (đśđóđŁ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%98%D0%A2%D0%9D

## Headline result

ITN (đśđ╝đ░ đóđ░đ║ĐŐđ▓ đŁđ░ĐÇđżđ┤ / There Is Such a People) took 23,861 votes (0.74%) from eleventh place ÔÇö down from 6.78% in October 2024 (7th position), a -6.05pp loss and -141,330 absolute votes. Slavi Trifonov's party fell out of parliament and is politically marginal.

## What worked

- Weak but even geography ÔÇö top-5 regions hold only 31.49% of the vote, meaning the party doesn't depend on a single source.
- Abroad over-index 1.17 ÔÇö the diaspora stayed close.
- 4 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö Slavi Trifonov is no longer the automatic leader everywhere. Hristinka Ivanova in Pleven (421 prefs) beat the local central names.

## What didn't work

- 0.74% ÔÇö effectively the end of the party. Zero state subsidy, zero parliamentary presence.
- A -6.05pp loss across all regions evenly ÔÇö Pleven -6.20, Ruse -6.02, Plovdiv -5.49, Razgrad, Targovishte. Systemic disintegration.
- Risk-section share ÔÇö 0.75% (over-index 1.02), compared to 7.45% in October 2024 ÔÇö a -6.70pp drop. ITN lost this base too.
- Against ACB (closest rival): 28 of 32 won ÔÇö so ITN is still larger than the other micro-parties, but out of parliament.

## Geographic strategy

For a party at 0.74%, geographic strategy does not exist. The strategy is survival ÔÇö preserving the structure for the next cycle or merging.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.75% at over-index 1.02 ÔÇö close to national, but absolute votes are under 250 across the whole network. Not material.

## Candidates and preferences

10,323 preferences, rate 43.26% (high for a falling party ÔÇö a loyal remnant). Top-1 4.08%. Hristinka Ivanova leads in Pleven (421), Slavi Trifonov in 25-MIR (380), Stanislav Balabanov in Plovdiv (335). 4 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö Trifonov is losing as the central name.

## Competitive geography

Against ACB: 28 won, 4 lost. Top margins: Vidin +0.90pp, Kyustendil +0.62. Losses: 23-MIR -0.53, 24-MIR -0.34. ITN leads in small towns against the new micro-parties but is invisible in Sofia.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Decision on continuation or wind-down.** At 0.74% and -6pp collapse, the campaign may not be viable. Leadership must decide.
- **Merger with another residual party.** ITN + Siyanie or ITN + ACB ÔÇö arithmetically insufficient to clear the threshold, but cheaper than a standalone structure.
- **Protect the local names.** Ivanova, Balabanov ÔÇö they preserved their own vote and can be assets for a new formation.
- **Do not rely on Slavi Trifonov.** The historic 25-30% from 2021 will not return. New identity or end.

### đÉđŤđśđÉđŁđí đŚđÉ đčđáđÉđĺđÉ đś đíđĺđ×đĹđ×đöđś ÔÇô đÉđčđí (đÉđčđí)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%90%D0%9F%D0%A1

## Headline result

APS (Alliance for Rights and Freedoms) took 50,759 votes (1.57%) from tenth place ÔÇö far below the 4% threshold. After the DPS split between Delyan Peevski and the Do─čan faction in 2024, APS was the political home of the post-Do─čan wing. The result is catastrophic: the Turkish minority APS hoped to consolidate transferred to PB.

## What worked

- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 2.40 ÔÇö structurally, APS remained a Turkish-minority party. 43.93% of the party vote comes from those 8 oblasts.
- Abroad over-index 2.36 ÔÇö the Turkish-origin diaspora stayed close.
- 12 ballot-order upsets out of 30 ÔÇö the post-DPS local networks function: Ahmed Vranchev in Blagoevgrad (621 prefs), Esra Ibish in Haskovo (446), Sevim Ali in Burgas (327). Local Turkish-community representatives have their own vote.
- Against ITN (closest rival in vote total): 18 of 32 won ÔÇö losing side of the parliamentary market, winning side of its own segment.

## What didn't work

- 1.57% ÔÇö failure. APS did not inherit a single point of DPS's 19% from October 2024.
- Collapse in traditional Turkish oblasts: Kardzhali -32.97pp (4.27% for APS vs 56% for DPS), Razgrad -32.11pp (5.24%), Silistra -18.13pp (6.00%). The community did not follow Do─čan.
- Risk-section share ÔÇö 2.13% (over-index 1.36, vs 12.21% for DPS before). A small residue.
- Sofia City over-index 0.11 ÔÇö essentially zero in the capital. APS does not exist outside its specific ethnic segment.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** Targovishte and Silistra ÔÇö the only places with positive margins over ITN. **Rebuild** Kardzhali and Razgrad ÔÇö but against DPS-Peevski on one side and PB on the other, resources required are enormous.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 2.13% in the 138 sections at over-index 1.36 ÔÇö above proportional, but absolute votes are small. Not a road to parliament.

## Candidates and preferences

12,745 preferences, rate 25.11%, top-1 4.87%. Ahmed Vranchev leads in Blagoevgrad (621), Esra Ibish in Haskovo (446), Sevim Ali in Burgas (327). 12 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö APS's central list has no mobilising power; local regional names are the principal asset.

## Competitive geography

Against ITN: 18 won, 14 lost. Top margins: Targovishte +6.09pp, Silistra +5.42. Losses: Vidin -0.94, Pleven -0.71. The real competitor for this base, however, is not ITN ÔÇö it is DPS-Peevski (for residual Turkish loyalty) and PB (for everyone who wanted change).

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate unification with DPS-Peevski.** APS + DPS = ~9% ÔÇö back to parliamentary weight. Standalone, both under 8%.
- **Promote the local winners.** Vranchev, Ibish, Ali ÔÇö they have an electorate; the central list does not.
- **Acknowledge the bloc loss.** The Turkish minority voted for PB. The next campaign cannot take this base for granted.
- **Concentrate resources in Targovishte and Silistra.** The only regions where APS leads in a standalone view.

### đÉđŁđóđśđÜđ×đáđúđčđŽđśđ×đŁđĽđŁ đĹđŤđ×đÜ (đÉđÜđĹ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%90%D0%9A%D0%91

## Headline result

ACB (Anti-Corruption Bloc) took 18,999 votes (0.59%) from twelfth place in its ballot debut. The party did not exist in October 2024; for a debut formation under a new identity, the result is symbolic ÔÇö no parliament, but a political brand declared.

## What worked

- Sofia City over-index 1.76 ÔÇö the strongest urban identity after PB and PP-DB. 33.70% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.16 ÔÇö Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas accept the brand.
- Toma Belev (known environmentalist and political activist) is the face: 474 preferences in 23-MIR, 4 ballot-order upsets. For a debut, a real bench with its own identity.
- Against BB (closest rival): 23 of 32 won.

## What didn't work

- 0.59% ÔÇö far from 4%. For a party with debut urban ambition, this is below potential.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.49 ÔÇö no connection to minority communities.
- Abroad over-index 1.07 ÔÇö close to proportional, but absolute numbers are negligible.
- Lost 9 regions to BB, all in north-west and central Bulgaria. The party is purely Sofia-based.

## Geographic strategy

For a party with debut 0.59% and an urban core, the geographic strategy is concentration. **Defend** Sofia City and Plovdiv, where over-indexes 1.76 and 1.16 show real brand presence. **Ignore** everything else ÔÇö wasting resources on a national campaign at this level is a loss.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 0.57% at over-index 0.97 ÔÇö almost no presence. Expected for an anti-corruption urban platform.

## Candidates and preferences

7,443 preferences, rate 39.18%, top-1 6.37%. Toma Belev in 23-MIR (474), Vasil Gyurov in 23-MIR (209), Konstantin Bachiyski in Burgas (203). 4 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö for a debut party, good local pull.

## Competitive geography

Against BB: 23 won, 9 lost. Top margins: Burgas +0.25pp, Abroad +0.21. Losses: Pernik -0.88, 24-MIR -0.44. Competition is between micro-parties and does not determine parliamentary chances.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate unification with Siyanie, BC or BB.** Four new urban parties split the same ~5% electorate. One merged could clear the threshold.
- **Develop Toma Belev as the principal face.** 4 upsets and own pull in 23-MIR ÔÇö foundation for the next campaign.
- **Focus exclusively on cities.** Over-index 1.76 in Sofia and 1.16 in big cities ÔÇö that is where the return is.
- **Don't build a national structure.** At 0.59%, regional branches are cost without revenue. Digital campaign, focused on urban identity.

### đčđč đĺđĽđŤđśđžđśđĽ (đĺđÁđ╗đŞĐçđŞđÁ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%92%D0%B5%D0%BB%D0%B8%D1%87%D0%B8%D0%B5

## Headline result

Velichie took 100,572 votes (3.10%) from seventh place ÔÇö down from 4.00% in October 2024 (9th position). Better positioning, no parliament. Minimal loss of -0.90pp at +3,075 absolute votes ÔÇö the party absorbed part of the turnout increase but not enough to clear 4%.

## What worked

- Climbed from 9th to 7th as competitors contracted (Vazrazhdane collapsed).
- Abroad over-index 1.86 ÔÇö one of the strongest diaspora over-indexes. 10.73% of the national vote comes from abroad.
- Mild gains in small central and western regions: Pazardzhik +0.89pp, Lovech +0.85, Gabrovo +0.75, Targovishte +0.68, Kyustendil +0.66 ÔÇö local-niche progress.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster +0.22pp ÔÇö the only positive there, against the trend. Small but exceptional.
- Yuliana Mateeva in Varna (5.28% of national prefs) and Ivelin Mihaylov in 25-MIR (4.25%) ÔÇö two local names with their own draw.

## What didn't work

- Did not cross 4%. Sixth or seventh result in a row below the threshold ÔÇö systemic wall, not bad campaign.
- Losses in big cities and Sofia MIRs: Varna -0.57pp, 25-MIR -0.17, Plovdiv -0.15, 23-MIR -0.15. The party does not break the urban liberal wall.
- Pollsters underestimated Velichie by 0.20 to 1.40pp (TR -1.40, GIB -1.16); only ML over-polled (+0.55). An under-poll for a threshold-edge party means the campaign worked in panic mode.
- Against BSP-UL (closest rival in vote total): 14 of 32 won, 18 lost ÔÇö the losing side.
- Only 1 ballot-order upset ÔÇö central list strong, bench thin outside Mihaylov.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** abroad ÔÇö the only field with double-digit over-indexing. **Attack** in small central and western regions (Lovech, Gabrovo, Kyustendil) where deltas are positive. **Concede** big cities and Sofia MIRs ÔÇö the party has no urban draw.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 3.27% at over-index 1.05 ÔÇö close to national. Maksuda 4.22%, Stolipinovo 2.76%, Dolno Ezerovo 4.21%. Small drop vs October 2024 (-0.97pp). Same as MECh ÔÇö these sections deliver under 1,000 votes for the party. Not a road to 4%.

## Candidates and preferences

34,447 preferences, rate 34.25%, top-1 5.28%. Yuliana Mateeva leads in Varna (1,820), Ivelin Mihaylov in 25-MIR (1,465), Pavel Stoimenov in Blagoevgrad (1,224), Yordan Mitsikulev in Pazardzhik (1,102), Krasimira Ninova-Katincharova in Stara Zagora (1,024). Only 1 ballot-order upset ÔÇö Mihail Dinev beat Ljubisha Blazhevski in Burgas. Central list dominates.

## Competitive geography

Against BSP-UL (closest rival): won 14, lost 18. Top margins: Abroad +4.84pp, Varna +1.92, Veliko Tarnovo +1.19. Losses: Yambol -2.60, Kyustendil -1.64, Sofia region -1.43. The two parties split the same pool, but BSP-UL has a wider small-town base.

## Polling intelligence

Six of seven agencies underestimated Velichie: AR -0.20pp, CAM -0.58, MY -0.90, SH -1.00, GIB -1.16, TR -1.40 ÔÇö only ML over-polled (+0.55). Systematic ~1pp under-poll ÔÇö the party took 1pp more than market expectations. A small buffer against the threshold, but too small to clear it.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Negotiate a coalition with MECh.** MECh + Velichie = 6.33% ÔÇö over the threshold. Standalone, both under 4%.
- **Defend abroad.** Over-index 1.86 is the party's asset. A diaspora-focused campaign could deliver +0.3pp nationally.
- **Develop Mihaylov and Mateeva.** Two faces with over 1,400 prefs each ÔÇö they can become visible leadership in the campaign.
- **Quit the urban contest.** Over-index 0.70 in Sofia City at +12pp turnout growth ÔÇö impossible to break through.
- **Reallocate to small central regions.** Positive deltas in Lovech, Gabrovo, Kyustendil show where the return is.

### đôđĽđáđĹ-đíđöđí

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%93%D0%95%D0%A0%D0%91-%D0%A1%D0%94%D0%A1

## Headline result

GERB-SDS took 433,755 votes (13.39%), placing a distant second behind PB (Progressive Bulgaria), which swept the election with 44.59% ÔÇö half GERB-SDS's October 2024 share (26.39%, position 1). The collapse is starker against turnout: with the electorate expanding from 38.81% to 50.70% (+11.89pp), the party still shed 208,766 absolute votes. Every new voter who showed up on April 19 went to PB ÔÇö the entire turnout surge was absorbed by the winner.

## What worked

- Held the regional leaders in the central-west (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa) ÔÇö leads of 11-14pp over PP-DB in areas where the urban liberal opposition has no organisational depth.
- Preference engagement was high (51.26% of voters cast a preferential vote), suggesting a list-loyal core that still showed up.
- Stronghold concentration is moderate (top-5 regions = 32.44% of national vote), so the loss is not concentrated in any single geography.
- Local figures over-performed central names in 13 of roughly 30 regions ÔÇö Stefan Apostolov in Blagoevgrad (6,860 prefs, beating Rosen Zhelyazkov by over 4,400), Gyunay Hyusmen in Razgrad (2,327 vs 306 for the list leader), Georgi Stankov in Haskovo (5,606 vs Delyan Dobrev's 2,991). The bench is real.

## What didn't work

- Lost 208,766 absolute votes in a +12pp turnout election ÔÇö the worst possible combination.
- The other three big cities (Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas) shed 8.40pp of vote share collectively. Urban erosion is structural, not a one-region story.
- Risk-neighborhood vote share fell from 36.12% to 11.41% ÔÇö a 24.71pp drop. GERB-SDS's traditional capacity to mobilise these sections has evaporated.
- Steep losses in the southern core: Vratsa -11.58pp, Dobrich -11.55pp, Smolyan -10.66pp, Haskovo -10.65pp, Lovech -9.70pp.
- Pollsters missed the collapse: every published agency over-polled GERB-SDS by 5-11pp, with GIB at +11.21pp and CAM at +10.93pp. The party walked into election night expecting a much better result.

## Geographic strategy

GERB-SDS is now an outside-the-big-cities party in everything but name. Sofia City delivered 13.25% (-4.56pp), and the Sofia-Plovdiv-Varna-Burgas axis combined gives the party 18.89% of its national total against 22.27% prior. **Defend** the central-west belt (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa, Blagoevgrad) where margins over PP-DB remain double-digit. **Attack** the smaller mixed-population oblasts (Razgrad, Shumen, Kardzhali) where the -6.80pp ethnic-mixed cluster delta is recoverable through local figures already proven at the polls. **Triage** the three Sofia constituencies and abroad ÔÇö losing margins of -19pp to -3pp; recovery there needs a different list and message, not an incremental fix.

## Risk neighborhoods

The collapse here is the single most striking number in the bundle: 36.12% Ôćĺ 11.41% share of votes cast in monitored Roma-neighborhood sections, an over-index ratio of 0.85 (now slightly below the party's national share). Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) gave 10.87%, Maksuda (26 sections, Varna) 12.11%, Pobeda (Burgas) the highest at 22.95%. Whatever ground operation produced 36% in October 2024 was either dismantled or out-organised by competitors.

## Candidates and preferences

Half the party's voters used a preferential vote (51.26% ÔÇö one of the highest engagement rates in the field). The top single candidate nationally is Boyko Borisov at 7,063 votes in 25-MIR Sofia, but only 3.18% of all party prefs ÔÇö striking dispersion. The list of local figures beating the central name is long: Stefan Apostolov (Blagoevgrad), Gyunay Hyusmen (Razgrad), Georgi Stankov (Haskovo), Martin Harizanov (Vratsa), Irena Dimova (Montana). 13 ballot-order upsets across roughly 30 regions tell a clear story: GERB-SDS is a federation of regional brands, not a Borisov-monolith party. The list strategy has to acknowledge this.

## Competitive geography

Against PP-DB ÔÇö the closest national rival in vote total ÔÇö GERB-SDS won 26 regions to 6 lost. But the six losses are the demographically decisive ones: Sofia 23, 24, 25 (-19, -13, -4pp), Plovdiv-city and abroad. Suburbanisation and youth turnout will keep pushing these regions further; the party cannot win a national plurality through the central-west belt alone.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies over-polled GERB-SDS: MY +5.11pp, TR +5.71, AR +6.11, SH +6.21, ML +7.79, CAM +10.93, GIB +11.21. CAM and GIB were the largest misses; the late-fieldwork agencies (MY 6d, TR 3d, AR 4d) clustered at +5-6pp. Historical bias is mildly positive across the board for GERB-SDS (TR +0.99, SH +1.08, AR +1.26, ML +1.47, GIB +1.84 over multiple cycles), but this cycle's overestimate is roughly 4├Ś the long-run pattern. The campaign was almost certainly making decisions with a 19-21% target in mind.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Treat April 2026 as a regime break, not a swing.** Losing 13pp in one cycle while turnout rose 12pp is structural, not tactical.
- **Rebuild the risk-neighborhood ground operation from scratch.** The 24.71pp collapse in those sections is the single biggest leakage and the cheapest to address with field investment.
- **Reorder the lists around proven local figures.** The 13 ballot-order upsets are a free roadmap ÔÇö lead with Apostolov in Blagoevgrad, Hyusmen in Razgrad, Stankov in Haskovo, Dimova in Montana.
- **Don't trust the polls.** Build internal tracking that adjusts for the 5-11pp systemic over-polling exposed in this cycle, or the next campaign will misallocate resources again.
- **Concede the urban liberal vote and pivot.** Sofia 23/24/25, Plovdiv-city and abroad are now competitive only with a different message ÔÇö don't waste a national campaign chasing them at the expense of the central-west belt.

### đöđ▓đŞđÂđÁđŻđŞđÁ đĚđ░ đ┐ĐÇđ░đ▓đ░ đŞ Đüđ▓đżđ▒đżđ┤đŞ - đöđčđí (đöđčđí)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%94%D0%9F%D0%A1

## Headline result

DPS took 230,693 votes (7.12%) and dropped to fourth ÔÇö down from 19% in October 2024, a -11.88pp loss and -231,807 absolute votes. Delyan Peevski's party held Kardzhali (56.16%) and Targovishte but lost almost everywhere else in its historically resilient ethnic-mixed base. Votes DPS had held for decades transferred to PB.

## What worked

- Kardzhali stayed a fortress: 56.16% and a +54.87pp lead over closest rival Vazrazhdane. The Turkish-minority vote held.
- The ethnic-mixed cluster stayed proportionally over-indexed: over-index 2.91, share 20.69%, contributing 53.16% of the party's national vote. The structural geography is intact, just shrunk.
- 24 ballot-order upsets out of 30 ÔÇö exceptional local decentralisation of the vote. Fatima Yaldas beat Delyan Peevski in Blagoevgrad (1,291 vs 462), Ismail Osman beat Kalin Stoyanov in Burgas, Aysel Mustafova crushed Nida Ahmedov in Shumen (1,568 vs 339). Local notables hold their own electorate independently of the central list.
- Paper voting at 86.61% ÔÇö second-highest in the field, marker of a loyal older / rural electorate.

## What didn't work

- Losses across traditional fortresses: Razgrad -24.39pp, Kardzhali -20.92pp, Targovishte -20.74pp, Silistra -14.46pp, Shumen. An entire belt eroded.
- Abroad -16.68pp ÔÇö the diaspora did not follow.
- Risk-section share fell from 12.21% to 2.35% (-9.86pp) ÔÇö over-index 0.33, now under-indexed. PB took this base at 50%+.
- Pollsters systematically overestimated the party: CAM +6.90pp, GIB +4.10, TR +3.08, SH +2.88. The campaign almost certainly worked with a 9-12% target.
- 24 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö flipped ÔÇö also mean the central list (i.e. Peevski) has no mobilising power outside specific municipalities.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** Kardzhali and Targovishte ÔÇö the only places with double-digit leads over rivals. **Rebuild** Razgrad, Silistra, Shumen ÔÇö where PB or others took votes DPS had held for decades. **Concede** the cities and abroad ÔÇö over-indexes of 0.11 in Sofia and 0.51 in big cities mean the party simply doesn't exist as an urban option.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share in the 138 monitored sections fell from 12.21% to 2.35%, a -9.86pp drop ÔÇö over-index 0.33, meaning DPS took less than a third of its national share in those sections. Stolipinovo 1.80%, Pobeda (Burgas) 10.86%, Filipovci 8.95%. Whatever organisational presence existed in Roma neighborhoods has collapsed. PB took the bloc at 50%+.

## Candidates and preferences

70,766 preferential votes, rate 30.68%, top-1 share only 2.26% ÔÇö extreme dispersion. 24 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö more than any other party. DPS's local networks function; the central list does not. Most telling: Fatima Yaldas (Blagoevgrad, 1,291 prefs) beat Delyan Peevski (462) ÔÇö the party leader lost his own district to a regional figure. Aysel Mustafova in Shumen took 1,568 vs 339 for Nida Ahmedov. Vasil Petkov in Pleven took 1,018 vs 419 for Dimitar Avramov. The party is a federation of regional brokers; Peevski is the name on the ballot, not a vote driver.

## Competitive geography

Against Vazrazhdane (closest rival in vote total): won 21 of 32, lost 11. Top margins: Kardzhali +54.87pp, Targovishte +22.02, Razgrad +16.75. Losses: Gabrovo -4.42, 25-MIR -4.18, 23-MIR -3.95 ÔÇö Sofia and the north are unfamiliar terrain for DPS. The real competitor for this base, however, is not Vazrazhdane ÔÇö it is PB.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies overestimated DPS. Errors: ML +0.53pp, MY +1.98, AR +2.28, SH +2.88, TR +3.08, GIB +4.10, CAM +6.90. Systematic ~3pp overestimate across the field, with CAM and GIB at over +4pp. The campaign entered election day expecting 9-12% and double the mandate count. Reality was different.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Acknowledge the loss of the Roma bloc as final.** -9.86pp in risk sections and the 12.21%-to-2.35% collapse mean the network is dismantled. Quick recovery will cost more than investment in a new identity.
- **Promote the local winners.** Yaldas, Mustafova, Osman, Petkov ÔÇö they belong at the top of next cycle's lists. They have an electorate; Peevski has less every cycle.
- **Defend Kardzhali with a local, not central, campaign.** The +54.87pp lead is a buffer, but Turkey and local Muslim leaders remain active ÔÇö not to be taken for granted.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 3pp overestimate ÔÇö next time, mark everything down.
- **Consider a coalition with the DPS family.** APS took 1.57% standalone. A combined list would land at 9-10% ÔÇö back to parliamentary weight.

### đĹđ¬đŤđôđÉđáđśđ» đťđ×đľđĽ (đĹđť)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%91%D0%9C

## Headline result

BC (Bulgaria Can) took 17,263 votes (0.53%) from fourteenth place in its ballot debut ÔÇö the last party above 0.5%. For a debut formation the result is symbolic; there is no standalone political future.

## What worked

- Sofia City over-index 1.71 ÔÇö an urban profile typical for a new city party. 32.58% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.11 ÔÇö Varna, Plovdiv, Burgas accept the brand modestly.
- Kuzman Iliev (known economist and media voice) is the face: 678 prefs in 25-MIR, 633 in Varna. For a debut ÔÇö a real leader's pull.
- Against BB (closest rival): 17 of 32 won ÔÇö near-tie in the micro-party field.

## What didn't work

- 0.53% ÔÇö barely above the registration threshold. No parliament, no state subsidy, no structural future.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.47 ÔÇö no breakthrough.
- Losses in north-western regions: Pernik -0.93pp vs BB, 24-MIR -0.60. Even in pure competition with other micro-parties, doesn't win.
- Only 2 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö the central list is strong, but the bench is thin outside Iliev.

## Geographic strategy

For a party at 0.53% with an urban core, the geographic strategy is concentration. **Defend** Sofia City and Varna, where over-indexes are highest. **Ignore** everything else.

Share of 0.59% at over-index 1.11 ÔÇö close to proportional, but absolute numbers are negligible.

## Competitive geography

Against BB: 17 won, 15 lost ÔÇö near-tie. Top margins: Abroad +0.18pp, Veliko Tarnovo +0.18. Losses: Pernik -0.93, 24-MIR -0.60. Micro-parties compete for the same droplet electorate.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Merge with ACB, Siyanie, BB.** Four new micro-parties with similar urban profiles compete for a ~5% combined electorate. One unified platform is the only path above 4%.
- **Develop Iliev as a leadership figure.** Top-1 12.39% means the central list works ÔÇö but absolutely it is under 700 prefs, so mobilising weight is low.
- **Don't build a national structure.** Digital campaign, focused on Sofia-Varna-Plovdiv, with resources commensurate with 0.5%.
- **Acknowledge the debut floor.** For a party with no history, 0.53% is a starting point, not an end. The next campaign must position between PB and PP-DB ÔÇö inaccessible territory, but better than disappearance.

### đíđśđ»đŁđśđĽ (đíđŞĐĆđŻđŞđÁ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%A1%D0%B8%D1%8F%D0%BD%D0%B8%D0%B5

## Headline result

Siyanie took 93,559 votes (2.89%) from ninth place in its ballot debut ÔÇö just below the 4% threshold, no parliament. The party did not exist in October 2024; for a debut campaign this is a notable result but insufficient.

## What worked

- For a debut ÔÇö almost the threshold. Only 1.11pp separates the party from a parliamentary seat; the next campaign starts with recognition, not from zero.
- Sofia City over-index 1.56 ÔÇö an urban profile typical for a new urban-protest party. 29.75% of the party vote comes from the three Sofia MIRs.
- Other big cities over-index 1.27 ÔÇö Varna, Plovdiv-city, Burgas accept the brand.
- Nikolay Popov leads in two MIRs: 23-MIR Sofia (3,965) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,772). A recognisable face with his own draw. Top-1 share 13.82% ÔÇö central list, but not catastrophically concentrated.
- Against BSP-UL (closest rival): won 8 of 32, lost 24 ÔÇö losing side, but not a rout.

- Weak periphery: Yambol -3.81pp (vs BSP-UL), Dobrich -2.40. Outside the cities ÔÇö almost nothing.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.48 ÔÇö no breakthrough to minority communities.

- Only 1 ballot-order upset ÔÇö the central list is strong, but the bench is thin outside Popov.

Against BSP-UL: 8 won, 24 lost. Top margins: 25-MIR +1.75pp, Plovdiv +1.65. Losses: Yambol -3.81, Dobrich -2.40. The two parties compete for differently-shaped electorates ÔÇö Siyanie is urban, BSP-UL is small-town.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Cross 4%.** For a debut party at 2.89% with an urban core, +1.5pp in Sofia and Plovdiv is a realistic target.
- **Build a bench beyond Popov.** 1 upset means nobody but the leader brings their own vote.
- **Don't waste resources in rural regions.** Over-indexes 0.48-0.71 in rural and diaspora regions ÔÇö negative ROI.
- **Prepare for coalition or merger with a similar new party.** Siyanie + ACB + BC = ~4% from a pure urban base.

### đčđáđ×đôđáđĽđíđśđĺđŁđÉ đĹđ¬đŤđôđÉđáđśđ» (đčĐÇđĹ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%9F%D1%80%D0%91

## Headline result

PB (Progressive Bulgaria) took 1,444,920 votes (44.59%) on its first appearance on the ballot, swept all 32 multi-member districts, and lapped second-place GERB-SDS (13.39%) by 31pp. Turnout surged from 38.81% to 50.70% (+11.89pp), and effectively the entire incremental electorate consolidated behind PB ÔÇö ex-president Rumen Radev's vehicle.

## What worked

- A 32-for-32 regional sweep with leads of 19-45pp over GERB-SDS. The smallest margin (Kardzhali +19.48pp) is larger than the entire GERB-SDS-to-PP-DB gap.
- Geographic distribution is unusually flat: top-5 regions hold only 28.10% of the national vote and top-25 municipalities 45.13%. PB is broadly mobilised, not stronghold-driven.
- Won 50.46% of votes in monitored Roma-neighborhood sections ÔÇö over-index 1.13 ÔÇö including 50.48% in Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) and 60.12% in Dolno Ezerovo (Burgas). The bloc GERB-SDS held with 36% in October 2024 transferred wholesale.
- Half a million preferential votes (522,478, prefRate 36.16%). The top candidate ÔÇö Radev in Burgas ÔÇö captured only 4.35% of national prefs. The bench is broad: Galab Donev (Pazardzhik), Ilin Dimitrov (Varna), Vladimir Nikolov (Plovdiv), Aleksandar Pulev (Stara Zagora), Encho Keryazov (Yambol).
- Pollsters underestimated by 4-15pp across all seven agencies ÔÇö competitors planned against a much smaller PB.

## What didn't work

For a debut sweep, "didn't work" is a thin category. The structural weaknesses:

- Sofia City under-indexed at 0.81 ÔÇö won, but proportionally weaker than the national average. The three Sofia constituencies returned 32-35% versus 44.59% nationally.
- Abroad under-indexed at 0.85 ÔÇö diaspora communication channels were thinner than domestic ones.
- Kardzhali the only oblast where PB placed second (24.33%, behind DPS at 47%+) ÔÇö the Turkish-minority vote held against the wave.
- Only 3 ballot-order upsets out of 30 ÔÇö the central list dominated almost everywhere, which is partly a strength but also means few local figures have built their own electorate beyond Radev.

## Geographic strategy

The party won everywhere; the question is where to consolidate and where the lead is fragile. **Defend** the central-north and north-east ring where margins over GERB-SDS exceed 38pp (Yambol, prov. Plovdiv, Veliko Tarnovo, Pleven, Dobrich). **Watch** Sofia City ÔÇö under-indexed at 0.81 and PP-DB, not GERB-SDS, is the closest rival there, a different competitive dynamic. **Build** in Kardzhali (the only loss) and across the ethnic-mixed cluster broadly: PB took 40.89%, over-index 0.92 ÔÇö the brand is acceptable but not dominant.

## Risk neighborhoods

PB took 50.46% of votes in the 138 monitored Roma-neighborhood sections ÔÇö over-index 1.13, the highest of any party in the field. Stolipinovo (71 sections, Plovdiv) gave 50.48%, Maksuda (26 sections, Varna) 49.44%, Dolno Ezerovo (Burgas) 60.12%, Fakulteta (Sofia) 53.73%. GERB-SDS held this bloc with a 36% national share; it transferred almost cleanly. Whoever ran the field operation deserves credit ÔÇö and ought to be retained.

## Candidates and preferences

Half a million preferential votes (522,478, prefRate 36.16%). The top candidate ÔÇö Rumen Radev ÔÇö took only 4.35% of national prefs because his votes split across two MIRs: 22,741 in Burgas (58.41% of regional prefs) and 21,541 in 25-MIR Sofia (75.78%). Beyond Radev the list draws on recognisable figures: Galab Donev (Pazardzhik), Ilin Dimitrov (Varna), Vladimir Nikolov (Plovdiv), Aleksandar Pulev (Stara Zagora), Encho Keryazov (Yambol). Only 3 ballot-order upsets out of 30 ÔÇö the central list held almost everywhere, which is both strength (discipline) and weakness (thin bench outside Radev and the presidential circle).

## Competitive geography

There is no real competitive contest in 2026. Against the closest rival GERB-SDS, PB won 32 of 32 regions with margins from +19.48pp (Kardzhali) to +45.25pp (Yambol). The narrowest leads ÔÇö Kardzhali, Blagoevgrad (+20pp), 23-MIR Sofia (+20pp), 24-MIR Sofia (+22pp), Lovech (+27pp) ÔÇö define where the next cycle's competitive map will form. None is currently lose-able, but PP-DB is the structural challenger in Sofia City; GERB-SDS or a rebuilt centre-right is the challenger in the central-west.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies under-polled PB ÔÇö by between 4.46pp (CAM) and 14.71pp (GIB). ML -8.36, SH -9.89, MY -9.99, AR -10.39, TR -11.39. Even the latest-fieldwork agencies (ML 3d, TR 3d, AR 4d) missed by 8-11pp. With no historical comparison (debut cycle), the cycle's bias is the entire picture. The systematic under-poll is the mirror image of GERB-SDS's over-poll: every published agency's model failed to capture either the PB wave or the new voters it brought in.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Do not read this as a baseline.** 44.59% at debut against a fragmented field with a halo candidate is a ceiling condition, not a floor. Expect normalisation toward the high 20s / low 30s in the next cycle if Radev does not lead.
- **Build the post-Radev bench now.** Top-1 share of 4.35% is structurally healthy, but only 3 ballot-order upsets means few local figures have built their own electorate. Two cycles from now this will matter.
- **Invest in Sofia City and the diaspora.** Both under-indexed at ~0.85; they are the missing piece of a true national majority and the most contested by PP-DB.
- **Hold the risk-neighborhood field operation.** A 50.46% share is the largest single-cycle bloc transfer in recent BG politics ÔÇö the operation that delivered it is institutional capital, not an artifact of the wave.
- **Manage the polling environment.** A 4-15pp under-poll across every agency in the debut cycle means the campaign was operating with a distorted picture of its own support; private tracking with safety margins is a one-cycle priority.

## Headline result

BB (Blue Bulgaria) took 18,640 votes (0.58%) from thirteenth place ÔÇö down from 1.07% in October 2024, a -0.49pp loss and -7,405 absolute votes. Petar Moskov's party preserved its identity but lost a quarter of an already minimal electorate.

## What worked

## What didn't work

- Losses in Sofia MIRs: 23-MIR -0.69pp, 24-MIR -0.60. Even in its own stronghold, BB is losing share.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster over-index 0.43 ÔÇö no breakthrough.
- Against ACB (closest rival): 9 of 32 won, 23 lost ÔÇö losing side against new urban competition.
- Abroad over-index 0.73 ÔÇö the diaspora does not recognise the brand.

Against ACB: 9 won, 23 lost. Top margins: Pernik +0.88pp, 24-MIR +0.44. Losses: Burgas -0.25, Abroad -0.20. ACB ÔÇö new, no history, similar urban profile ÔÇö beats BB almost everywhere. A signal of an expired brand.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Merge with ACB or BC.** Three parties with similar socio-liberal profiles compete for the same sub-1% electorate. A meaningful coalition is the only path.
- **Develop Moskov and Lilkov as platforms.** They have their own vote; the party brand does not.
- **Acknowledge the position.** BB was the centre-right party of the 2010s. In 2026 that electorate is at PP-DB or PB. New identity or shutdown.

## Headline result

Nikolay Radulov 968 in Varna. Kiril Veselinski 887 in Blagoevgrad. Only 1 ballot-order upset ÔÇö the central list is accepted, but the bench is thin outside Vasilev.

## Recommendations for next campaign

### đĹđíđč ÔÇô đ×đĹđĽđöđśđŁđĽđŁđÉ đŤđĽđĺđśđŽđÉ (đĹđíđč-đ×đŤ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%91%D0%A1%D0%9F-%D0%9E%D0%9B

## Headline result

BSP-UL (BSP-UL ÔÇô United Left) took 97,753 votes (3.02%) from eighth place in its debut coalition format. This is the first time in modern Bulgarian history that a BSP-successor party is below the 4% threshold and out of parliament. Regional drops vs the prior cycle, measured against the consolidated party list, range from -2 to -4.4pp.

## What worked

- A national-map presence preserved ÔÇö the party did not vanish despite structural erosion.
- A modest result in Sofia City: over-index 1.05, share 3.18% ÔÇö the only place where BSP-UL is above proportional. The capital's class electorate held.
- 4 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö a bench with local pull: Mincho Kazandzhiev in Lovech (520 vs 302), Todor Atanasov in Targovishte, Pavel Karaivanov in Shumen, Genadi Tsitlakidis in Gabrovo. Regional leftists with their own vote.
- Gergana Ormanlieva in Blagoevgrad ÔÇö top-1 candidate with 4.73% of national preferences.
- GIB nearly exact (+0.11pp error) ÔÇö for a threshold-edge party, at least one pollster delivered the true value.

## What didn't work

- Below 4%. BSP is out of parliament for the first time in history. An institutional catastrophe.
- Heavy losses in north-central regions: Pleven -4.39pp, Targovishte -4.36, prov. Plovdiv -4.14, Pazardzhik -4.00, Kyustendil -3.70. Small towns historically left-leaning turned to PB.
- Abroad over-index 0.31 ÔÇö essentially no diaspora support. That is an urban-western trend and BSP-UL has no channels.
- Risk-section share ÔÇö 2.03% (over-index 0.67) ÔÇö under-indexed. Not a traditional field but also not a new reserve.
- Against Velichie (closest rival): won 18 of 32, lost 14 ÔÇö the winning side, but no parliamentary bonus.
- Pollsters systematically overestimated: CAM +2.25pp, SH +1.58, AR +0.98, MY +0.98, TR +0.98 ÔÇö only ML (-0.67) and GIB (+0.11) were close. The campaign expected 4-4.5%; reality was 3.02%.

## Geographic strategy

For a party out of parliament, geographic strategy shifts to survival. **Defend** Lovech, Kyustendil, Sofia region ÔÇö the only regions with positive margins over Velichie. **Rebuild** Pleven, Targovishte, prov. Plovdiv, Pazardzhik ÔÇö where 4pp packet drops are most painful. **Concede** abroad and Kardzhali (over-index under 0.4) ÔÇö no return there.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share of 2.03% at over-index 0.67 ÔÇö below proportional. Stolipinovo 2.43%, Maksuda 1.76%, Dolno Ezerovo 1.79%. BSP historically held a share of these communities; not anymore. PB took the bloc at 50%+.

## Candidates and preferences

42,740 preferences, rate 43.72% (high for a small party), top-1 4.73%. Gergana Ormanlieva leads in Blagoevgrad (2,021), Krum Zarkov in 24-MIR (1,421) and Burgas (721), Tatyana Doncheva in Plovdiv (1,121), Gabriel Valkov in 23-MIR (884). 4 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö Kazandzhiev beat Berievski in Lovech 520-302; Karaivanov beat Jablianov (party leader!) in Shumen 309-177. Another signal that central names are weaker than regional ones.

## Competitive geography

Against Velichie: 18 won, 14 lost. Top margins: Yambol +2.60pp, Kyustendil +1.64, Sofia region +1.43. Losses: Abroad -4.86, Varna -1.93, Veliko Tarnovo -1.19. Small central and southern regions are better terrain for BSP-UL than the cities.

## Polling intelligence

Agencies trended mostly positive: GIB +0.11pp (nearly exact), ML -0.67, AR +0.98, MY +0.98, TR +0.98, SH +1.58, CAM +2.25. Mild systematic 1pp overestimate ÔÇö five agencies had BSP-UL +1 to +2pp above the actual. The campaign expected to clear the threshold; missed by 1pp.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Decide on unification or new identity.** BSP-UL outside parliament means the coalition format must be reconsidered. Atanas Zafirov and the leadership must choose ÔÇö traditional BSP or a new left.
- **Develop the regional faces.** Kazandzhiev, Karaivanov, Tsitlakidis ÔÇö local networks with their own electorate. The central list does not work.
- **Defend urban class voting.** Sofia City over-index 1.05 ÔÇö only there does BSP-UL have a proportional electorate above national.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 1-1.5pp overestimate ÔÇö next campaign must mark down and manage internal expectations.
- **Consider an alliance with PP-DB or PB.** For a party out of parliament, going alone is more expensive than concession. BSP-UL + PB on a joint list in specific MIRs may be electorally rational.

### đÜđ×đÉđŤđśđŽđśđ» đčđáđ×đöđ¬đŤđľđÉđĺđÉđťđĽ đčđáđ×đťđ»đŁđÉđóđÉ ÔÇô đöđĽđťđ×đÜđáđÉđóđśđžđŁđÉ đĹđ¬đŤđôđÉđáđśđ» (đčđč-đöđĹ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%9F%D0%9F-%D0%94%D0%91

## Headline result

PP-DB took 408,846 votes (12.62%) and slid to third ÔÇö behind PB (44.59%) and GERB-SDS (13.39%) ÔÇö from second with 14.21% in October 2024. The paradox: vote share fell 1.60pp but absolute votes ROSE by 62,772 in a +12pp turnout election. The urban base deepened; the national space realigned around PB.

## What worked

- The three Sofia MIRs delivered the strongest gains: 23-MIR +6.44pp (to 31.52%), 24-MIR +5.05pp (to 26.50%), 25-MIR +3.51pp (to 17.70%). The urban liberal vote consolidated.
- Abroad +6.80pp (to 22.84%) ÔÇö the diaspora moved to PP-DB against the general PB tide. Abroad delivers 10.43% of the party's national vote.
- Over-index 2.06 in Sofia City and 1.81 abroad ÔÇö PP-DB is the urban liberal brand by definition, no ambiguity.
- Machine voting 76.07% ÔÇö the highest paper-machine inversion in the field, reflecting a young / urban / tech-literate electorate.
- 186,123 preferential votes (rate 45.52%, one of the highest) with 11 ballot-order upsets ÔÇö Bozhidar Bozhanov beat Nikolay Denkov in 23-MIR Sofia (13,528 vs 9,640), Anna Bodakova beat Ivaylo Mirchev in 24-MIR, Stela Nikolova beat Pavel Popov in Varna. The bench has its own pull, not just the central list.
- Pollsters were close (errors -1.42 to +2.35pp); the campaign worked with realistic expectations.

## What didn't work

- Concentration is extreme: 56.18% of the national vote comes from 5 regions and 65.32% from 25 municipalities. PP-DB is essentially absent across most of the country.
- Ethnic-mixed cluster: over-index 0.55, share 6.91%. The party has no bridge to these communities.
- In risk neighborhoods ÔÇö share 11.37% (over-index 0.90), almost unchanged from 11.83% in October 2024. PB now holds Stolipinovo at 50%; PP-DB cannot compete for that electorate.
- Against GERB-SDS: lost 26 of 32 regions; won only 6 (the three Sofia MIRs, abroad, Plovdiv-city, 25-MIR by a thin margin). Outside the urban liberal core, GERB-SDS leads by double digits: Lovech -13.52pp, Montana -12.33pp, Blagoevgrad -11.88pp.
- Vote-share losses in small conservative-leaning regions: Smolyan -2.06pp, Silistra -0.94pp, Haskovo -0.62pp. Erosion at the periphery.

## Geographic strategy

PP-DB is a party of Sofia, the diaspora and the big cities ÔÇö full stop. **Defend** the three Sofia MIRs, abroad and Plovdiv-city ÔÇö where the party leads or is close. **Concede** central-west and northern Bulgaria (Lovech, Montana, Vratsa) ÔÇö losses there run double-digit and are not quickly recoverable. **Experiment** in Burgas (8.72%) and Varna (13.12%) ÔÇö both index below what a 12.62% national party should hold in those urban markets.

## Risk neighborhoods

PP-DB took 11.37% in the 138 monitored sections, over-index 0.90 ÔÇö close to the national share. Stolipinovo gave 11.81%, Maksuda 13.09%, Filipovci 16.18%. Change vs October 2024: only -0.46pp. PP-DB did not lose ground here but had no operation to capture it either. PB took 50%+ of these sections.

## Candidates and preferences

High engagement: 45.52% of voters cast a preference. The top candidate ÔÇö Bozhidar Bozhanov (former e-government minister) ÔÇö took 13,528 preferences in 23-MIR Sofia (7.27% of national party prefs), beating former PM Nikolay Denkov (9,640). Politically significant: PP-DB voters preferred the technocrat over the party leader. Other key names: Elisaveta Belobradova (9,864 in 23-MIR), Anna Bodakova (6,843 in 24-MIR, beating Ivaylo Mirchev), Aleksandar Simidchiev (4,531 in 25-MIR, beating Boyko Rashkov). 11 ballot-order upsets means the bench has its own electoral standing.

## Competitive geography

Against GERB-SDS (closest national rival): won 6 of 32 regions, lost 26. The wins are almost all urban-liberal: 23-MIR +19.03pp, abroad +18.17pp, 24-MIR +13.05pp, 25-MIR +3.57pp, Plovdiv-city +3.25pp. The losses span a wide periphery: Lovech -13.52pp, Montana -12.33pp, Blagoevgrad -11.88pp ÔÇö a belt where PP-DB has no organisational presence.

## Polling intelligence

Agencies were close on PP-DB: ML +0.56pp, AR -1.02, SH -1.02, GIB -1.19, MY -1.22, TR -1.42, CAM +2.35. Six agencies mildly under-polled by 1-1.5pp; only CAM over-polled, at +2.35. Far less drift than for PB (-4 to -15pp) or GERB-SDS (+5 to +11pp). The campaign's polling picture was credible.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Accept the identity and invest in it.** PP-DB is the urban liberal alternative to PB. Trim national ambitions in favour of depth in Sofia, abroad and the big cities.
- **Promote Bozhanov and the next generation.** The 11 ballot-order upsets show the electorate rewards individual figures over party leaders. Use it.
- **Don't chase the ethnic-mixed cluster.** Over-index 0.55 at national-campaign cost is negative ROI. Cede those regions to the DPS-APS family and PB.
- **Prepare for the next contest against PB, not GERB-SDS.** In 23-MIR and 24-MIR, PB is now the principal rival. The 2026 strategy aimed at GERB-SDS became obsolete on April 19.
- **Defend abroad aggressively.** +6.80pp in the diaspora at +0.81 national activity there is a strong result ÔÇö but PB took 38% there. It will be attacked.

### đĺđ¬đŚđáđÉđľđöđÉđŁđĽ (đĺĐŐđĚĐÇđ░đÂđ┤đ░đŻđÁ)

URL: https://electionsbg.com/en/party/%D0%92%D1%8A%D0%B7%D1%80%D0%B0%D0%B6%D0%B4%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%B5

## Headline result

Vazrazhdane took 137,940 votes (4.26%) and barely cleared the 4% threshold from fifth place ÔÇö down from 13.36% in October 2024 (third position), a -9.11pp loss and -187,418 votes. One of the largest losses in the field: Kostadinov's party held parliamentary presence at the cost of two-thirds of its electorate.

## What worked

- Cleared the threshold. Given the depth of the collapse, that is a political victory in itself ÔÇö preserves the structure for the next cycle.
- Abroad over-index 1.23 ÔÇö the diaspora stayed proportionally stronger than the national average. 7.10% of the party vote comes from abroad, more than from several larger parties.
- Kostadinov held the facade: 5.29% of national prefs, leader in Varna (2,568) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,476). For a party in free fall, the leader stayed recognisable.
- Polling agencies overestimated the party by 1-4pp ÔÇö the campaign entered the day expecting 5-8%; reality was 4.26%, but not a catastrophe.

## What didn't work

- A -9.11pp loss and -187,418 votes in a +12pp turnout election ÔÇö new voters did not appear for the nationalist option; old ones left.
- Heavy drops in central and eastern Bulgaria: Yambol -7.67pp, Stara Zagora -7.45, Dobrich -7.13, Veliko Tarnovo -7.02, Gabrovo -6.94. The party collapsed in its own strongholds.
- Risk-section share fell from 13.81% to 4.84% (-8.97pp) ÔÇö Vazrazhdane also held a slice of the Roma sections; it transferred to PB.
- 0 ballot-order upsets out of 30 ÔÇö total dominance of the central list. When Kostadinov loses, the party has no local figures with their own votes to take the relay.
- Against new competition from MECh (close in ideology): won only 29 of 32 regions, but with minimal margins ÔÇö Varna +3.19pp, Veliko Tarnovo +1.81, Dobrich +1.81. That is not a safe lead; it is MECh's breakthrough everywhere.

## Geographic strategy

**Defend** the 4% threshold above everything else. **Rebuild** in central-east Bulgaria (Yambol, Stara Zagora, Dobrich), where the party lost 7pp in a single cycle. **Concede** the urban national-conservative space to MECh and Siyanie ÔÇö they are growing from a low base but the count keeps rising.

## Risk neighborhoods

Share fell from 13.81% to 4.84%, a -8.97pp drop ÔÇö almost identical to DPS's. The over-index stays at 1.14 (slightly over-indexed), but the absolute votes transferred to PB. Maksuda (Varna) gave 6.43%, Stolipinovo 4.29%, Dolno Ezerovo 5.32%. Vazrazhdane has no field operation to rebuild this base.

## Candidates and preferences

48,545 preferences, rate 35.19%, top-1 share 5.29% ÔÇö concentrated around Kostadinov. He leads in two MIRs: Varna (2,568) and 25-MIR Sofia (2,476). Tsoncho Ganev ÔÇö the party's #2 ÔÇö takes 1,825 in 23-MIR Sofia and 1,180 in Burgas. Iskra Mihaylova in Stara Zagora (1,234) ÔÇö the only female face in the top 5. Zero ballot-order upsets means the central list is absolute, but also that the party has no bench to succeed the leader.

## Competitive geography

Against MECh (closest rival): won 29 of 32, lost 3. Top margins: Varna +3.19pp, Veliko Tarnovo +1.81, Dobrich +1.81. Losses: Vratsa -0.86pp, Lovech -0.51, Pleven -0.37. The thin margins show MECh is the real threat next cycle ÔÇö one wobble and Vazrazhdane could fall out.

## Polling intelligence

All seven agencies overestimated the party: ML +0.68pp, AR +1.54, GIB +2.54, TR +2.84, MY +3.14, SH +3.74, CAM +4.48. Systematic 1-4pp inflation ÔÇö the campaign expected 6-8%. The polling model captured stated support but not actual late-cycle voting for the nationalist option, which clearly collapsed in the final weeks ÔÇö votes that PB absorbed.

## Recommendations for next campaign

- **Build a bench beyond Kostadinov.** Zero upsets at -9pp collapse means there is no successor. If Kostadinov steps back, the party drops to 1-2%.
- **Defend the 4% line with a focused campaign in strongholds.** Yambol, Stara Zagora, Dobrich, V. Tarnovo ÔÇö that is where the -7pp collapse was. A 2pp recovery there alone means 4.5-5% nationally.
- **Distrust the polls.** Systematic 2-4pp overestimate ÔÇö next campaign must mark down and manage expectations.
- **Accept the Roma-share loss.** Recovery against 50%+ PB is expensive. Better to segment: national-conservative votes in small towns.
- **Consider a coalition with MECh or Siyanie.** The three parties combined are 10.50% ÔÇö solid parliamentary weight. Standalone, each is under 5%.

### Machine-only voting: who wins and who loses

**Summary:** An interactive what-if on Bulgaria's own election data. Since 2021 every section records machine and paper votes separately ÔÇö the same electorate split only by voting medium, which makes the split a natural experiment. We remove the paper ballot in every 'large' section (above a chosen threshold), recast its paper-voters onto that section's machine distribution, and watch national vote share and parliamentary seats recompute live. Sliders control the threshold (100/200/300/500 voters) and a turnout drop-off; the pattern is consistent ÔÇö đôđĽđáđĹ and đöđčđí lose, đčđč-đöđĹ gains.

# Machine-only voting: who wins and who loses

> **This article is interactive.** On the live page you can set a section-size threshold and a turnout drop-off, and the vote-share bars, the parliamentary seat allocation and a district-by-district map recompute instantly against the most recent election. What follows is the method and the headline findings.

Since 2021 every Bulgarian parliamentary section has recorded **machine votes and paper votes side by side** ÔÇö the same electorate, on the same day, split only by the medium each voter chose. That split is a natural experiment: within a single section, machine-voters and paper-voters picked parties in measurably different proportions.

This lets us ask a concrete reform question. **What if paper ballots were removed in every "large" section ÔÇö above some number of registered voters ÔÇö forcing those voters onto the machine?**

This is not merely hypothetical. On 7 July 2026 the governing party, Progressive Bulgaria (đčĐÇđĹ), submitted a bill to parliament proposing exactly this ÔÇö fully machine voting, with paper kept only in sections under 300 voters (plus mobile, hospital and ship sections) ÔÇö [as reported here](https://www.focus-news.net/novini/Bylgaria/Izcyalo-mashinno-glasuvane-s-izklyuchenie-na-malkite-sekcii-predlaga-Progresivna-Bulgariya-2992060). The interactive tool tests what that reform would have done to the most recent result; đčĐÇđĹ's own bill draws the line at 300.

## The model

For each section above the chosen threshold that also has real machine votes, we treat the observed machine-voters as revealing that section's preference, and recast its paper-voters onto that same machine-vote distribution:

```
machineShare_p = machineVotes_p / ╬ú machineVotes
paperShare_p   = paperVotes_p   / ╬ú paperVotes
votes_p(d)     = machineVotes_p + (1 Ôłĺ d) ┬Ě (paperTotal ┬Ě machineShare_p + invalid ┬Ě paperShare_p)
```

The turnout dial **d** is the share of a section's paper-voters who *abstain* rather than switch to a machine. At `d = 0` turnout is held constant; at `d = 100%` every paper-voter in a large section stays home and only the original machine-voters count.

A machine also won't accept a spoiled ballot, so the model recovers each affected section's invalid paper ballots (about 3.9% of paper in 2026) and adds them as valid votes, distributed by that section's **paper-vote shares** ÔÇö because the voters who mis-mark ballots belong to the same older, paper-preferring demographic (Fujiwara 2015). This feeds the paper-heavy parties and softens the swing (at the default it turns đčđč-đöđĹ's seat gain from +12 to +11 and đôđĽđáđĹ-đíđöđí's loss from Ôłĺ12 to Ôłĺ11).

Smaller sections ÔÇö and the few large sections whose machine failed ÔÇö are left exactly as recorded. We then re-aggregate nationally and run a Hare-quota seat allocation (4% threshold) on both the actual and the modelled totals.

## What we already excluded

Three parliamentary elections (July 2021, November 2021, October 2022) were **fully machine-only** ÔÇö they have no paper votes to redistribute, so they are outside this exercise. The five elections in this analysis (April 2021, April 2023, June 2024, October 2024, April 2026) all had real voter choice between the two media; the live tool runs the scenario on the most recent of them.

## The headline finding

The direction is remarkably stable across every election: **machine voting favours urban/reform parties, paper voting favours đôđĽđáđĹ and đöđčđí.** Forcing large sections onto the machine consistently:

- **cuts đôđĽđáđĹ-đíđöđí by roughly 4ÔÇô6 points** and đöđčđí by 1ÔÇô3 points;
- **lifts đčđč-đöđĹ by roughly 4ÔÇô6 points**, plus smaller gains for reform/protest parties;
- in 2023 and 2026 it flips the second-place finisher (đčđč-đöđĹ overtakes đôđĽđáđĹ); in October 2024 it knocks a party below the 4% line.

This direction is backed by a separate real-data analysis: in a recent election machine voting was chosen by 80% of đśđóđŁ, 79% of đčđč-đöđĹ and 70% of đĺĐŐđĚĐÇđ░đÂđ┤đ░đŻđÁ voters, while đôđĽđáđĹ, đöđčđí and đĹđíđč voters leaned to paper ([Radio Free Europe](https://www.svobodnaevropa.bg/a/32352096.html)).

The likely reason is who each group is: the machine is preferred by younger, urban voters, paper by older voters and people in smaller places ÔÇö so removing paper amplifies the urban/reform vote. By district, đčđč-đöđĹ's gain is biggest in Sofia and Plovdiv (up 5ÔÇô7 points), and there is exactly one winner flip ÔÇö Sofia's 23rd district, from đčĐÇđĹ to đčđč-đöđĹ. The regional map colours each district by its projected winner.

## What this is not

- The model combines two channels ÔÇö the **composition (selection) effect** (from which medium each voter chose) and the spoiled-ballot recovery above. It still is not the full effect of mandating machines, which would also shift turnout and carry the machine's own influence on the vote.
- It assumes paper-voters would vote like their section's machine-voters ÔÇö it captures the selection skew between the groups. The machine's on-screen flow nudges behaviour (the explicit "I support no one" button is picked by 1.8% of machine-voters vs 1.3% on paper) and can create errors of its own (Zucco & Nicolau, 2016).
- The spoiled-ballot recovery rests on an assumption: recovered invalid ballots are distributed by each section's paper-vote shares because mis-marking voters resemble the paper-preferring demographic (Fujiwara 2015), but a spoiled ballot carries no recorded preference, so the true split is unknowable.
- **The natural experiment is only as strong as machine adoption.** In April 2021 machine was a freely-chosen minority (~29% of affected voters), so its voters skew young/urban/early-adopter ÔÇö read that election as the most aggressive extrapolation, not the most reliable.
- The turnout drop-off is a scenario dial, not an estimate. In Bulgaria's three machine-only elections (2021ÔÇô2022) turnout was 39ÔÇô42%, within the range of the mixed elections around them (34ÔÇô51%), so a large machine-driven turnout collapse is not visible in the data ÔÇö though repeat-election fatigue confounds the comparison. Small drop-offs are the more likely case.
- Seats are allocated by the national Hare-Niemeyer quota with the 4% threshold ÔÇö the same method Bulgaria uses to fix each party's national total (it reproduces the official result for every election since 2013). Bulgaria then spreads those totals across the 31 districts, which only changes where seats land, not how many each party wins; the meaningful figure is the actual-vs-model *difference*.

## Further reading

- Fujiwara, T. (2015). [Voting Technology, Political Responsiveness, and Infant Health: Evidence from Brazil](https://onlinelibrary.wiley.com/doi/abs/10.3982/ECTA11520). *Econometrica* 83(2).
- Zucco, C. & Nicolau, J. (2016). [Trading old errors for new errors? The impact of electronic voting technology on party label votes in Brazil](https://www.sciencedirect.com/science/article/abs/pii/S0261379416301238). *Electoral Studies* 43.

**Summary:** The first regular budget of the Radev cabinet arrives with a 5.7%-of-GDP deficit and an excessive-deficit procedure just months after euro adoption. We line up the verified figures from the 2026 Budget Law and the 2026ÔÇô2028 medium-term forecast, gather the reactions of politicians and economists (sourced line by line), and run the claims themselves through our budget simulator: the deficit, the ÔéČ2,300 social-security cap and the party-subsidy cut all check out; 'you can't consolidate while debt explodes' is arithmetically false; and the 'soft' revenue and the 'Videnov-era' comparison do not survive scrutiny.
